{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 19:43:40","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:43:40","title":"Architectural Gifs Restore Damaged Cultural Sites Around the World","link":"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/?p=131854","description":"<div id=\"attachment_132969\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-132969\" class=\"wp-image-132969 size-full\" src=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/01_Hatra-Reconstruction.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"675\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-132969\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Hatra, Al-Jazīrah, Iraq</p></div>\n<p>Evoking a bit of time-travel, <a href=\"https://neomam.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">NeoMam</a> (<a href=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/2018/03/ancient-ruins-reconstructed-with-architectural-gifs/\">previously</a>) recently animated <a href=\"https://www.budgetdirect.com.au/blog/reconstructing-6-unesco-cultural-sites-in-danger-of-disappearing-forever.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a series</a> of gifs that restore impressive, human-made structures around the globe to pristine condition. Although the six landmarks are now in some form of decay and have made UNESCO&#8217;s <a href=\"https://whc.unesco.org/en/danger/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">list of endangered world heritage</a>, the short clips digitally reconstruct the sites to show what they&#8217;d look like had they not faced the ravages of time.</p>\n<p>Included in this round of restoration are a remnant of <a href=\"https://whc.unesco.org/en/news/1309/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Hatra</a>, a large fortified city that was capital of the first Arab Kingdom, and the hundreds of islets that make up <a href=\"https://whc.unesco.org/en/list/1503\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Nan Modol</a> in Micronesia. UNESCO designated these landmarks in danger because of natural and human-generated threats like earthquakes, military conflict, and urbanization. Dig into the history behind <a href=\"https://www.budgetdirect.com.au/blog/reconstructing-6-unesco-cultural-sites-in-danger-of-disappearing-forever.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the six restorations</a>, which were completed in partnership with BudgetDirect and architect Jelena Popovic, in addition to other at-risk locations on <a href=\"https://whc.unesco.org/en/list/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">UNESCO&#8217;s site</a>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div id=\"attachment_132973\" style=\"width: 1210px\" 19:43:40","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:43:40","title":"Paper Wildlife Sculptures by Artist Diana Beltrán Herrera Document Nature’s Most Striking https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/herrera-3-640x557@2x.jpg 1280w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/herrera-3-960x835@2x.jpg 1920w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/herrera-3-624x543@2x.jpg 1248w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2000px) 100vw, 2000px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-132948\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">All images © Diana Beltrán Herrera, shared with permission</p></div>\n<p>In 2012, Bristol-based artist <a href=\"http://www.dianabeltranherrera.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Diana Beltrán Herrera</a> (<a href=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/?s=Diana+Beltran+Herrera\">previously</a>) began sculpting impeccably layered paper birds and other wildlife as a way to record her surroundings. Her lifelike pieces continuously have captured nature&#8217;s finely detailed and minuscule elements, like the fibrous texture of feathers and the veins running through leaves.</p>\n<p>Today, the artist has expanded the practice to include exotic species and environments she&#8217;s never seen up close, developing her paper techniques to express the more nuanced details of the shapes and textures she studies in biology books. Now focusing on the structural elements of fungi, fruit, and florals, Beltrán Herrera shares with Colossal:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Paper as a medium for documentation allows me to register and create notions and ideas of subjects that I have not experienced in real life but that I can experience when a sculpture is completed. I like this approach because it is not harmful, and through my work, I can show and tell my viewers about the things I have been learning, of the importance of nature just by researching and making it myself.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Much of her work centers on conservation efforts and environmental justice. For example, a recent commission by Greenpeace UK bolstered the organization&#8217;s <a href=\"https://outlandish.com/project/greenpeace-plastic-free-rivers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Plastic Free Rivers</a> campaign. &#8221; I am constantly looking for more subjects that are relevant to the times we are living in, so that through my work I can communicate important information that can educate or just make things more visible. The approach is very (graphic) and visual, which helps to deliver a message,&#8221; she says.</p>\n<p>Beltrán Herrera&#8217;s upcoming projects include a commission for a coral sculpture, in addition to plans to launch a studio with her brother by the end of 2020. Her hope is to merge graphic and digital design with her paper pieces, potentially adding in animation, as well. Ultimately, her goal is to dive into larger projects. &#8220;I don&#8217;t see my work as something I want to know how to make and stay safe, but as a challenge, that will always allow me to wonder how to execute and create things that were never made with paper,&#8221; she says.</p>\n<p>To see more of Beltrán Herrera&#8217;s creative process and follow her future pieces, head to <a href=\"https://www.behance.net/pine\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Behance</a> and <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/dianabeltranherrera/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-132952\" src=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/herrera-7-scaled.jpg\" alt=\"\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Maori Sakai</a> imbues a bit of whimsy into otherwise mundane scenes through her delicately illustrated animations. Each gif is rendered largely in pastels and captures simple movements: a record spinning on a turntable, rain falling outside a window, and butterflies hovering around hydrangeas. Many of Sakai&#8217;s short animations, in addition to glimpses into her process, can be found on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/maori_sakai_illustration/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a> and <a href=\"https://maorisakai.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Tumblr</a>. class=\"wp-caption-text\">All images © Tortik Annushka, shared with permission</p></div>\n<p><a href=\"https://tortik-annuchka.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Tortik Annushka</a>’s fondant-wrapped desserts more closely resemble luxurious, edible artworks than the buttercream sheet cakes available from grocery bakeries. Based in Moscow, the confectionary designs lavish pastries that mimic a tub of ice cream, asymmetric sculptures, and famous paintings. Each pristinely shaped tier is made by hand entirely from scratch.</p>\n<p>Founded in 2009 by a brother and sister, Torik Annushka hopes to offer more workshops and open a spot to enjoy the luxurious sweets in the future. You can follow the family business&#8217;s delightful creations on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/tortikannuchka/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a>. (via <a href=\"https://www.swiss-miss.com/2020/07/designer-cakes.html?utm_source=feedburner&#38;utm_medium=feed&#38;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Swissmiss+%28swissmiss%29\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener Great Britain. 2003.</p></div>\n<p>In collaboration with <em>Vogue</em>, <a href=\"https://www.magnumphotos.com/shop/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Magnum Photos</a> just launched a massive print sale with half of all proceeds being donated to the <a href=\"https://www.naacp.org/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">NAACP</a>. Included in the collection of archival photographs are <a href=\"http://philippehalsman.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Philippe Halsman</a>’s iconic portrait of Angela Davis, <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/thomashoepker/?hl=tr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Thomas Hoepker</a>’s shot of Muhammed Ali, and dozens of other images that fall under the theme of solidarity. Many of the pieces explore the power of human bonds, about which organizers say:</p>\n<blockquote><p>While acknowledging the daunting divisions and fault-lines running through society, the selection will examine a simultaneous human yearning for commune and connection, aiming to explore the strength of both the individual and collective, as well as the interdependence of peoples around the world in the face of adversity and oppression.</p></blockquote>\n<p>All 6 x 6-inch prints are signed or estate-stamped, museum-quality, and available for $100. Find some of Colossal&#8217;s favorites below—which includes <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Cole_(photographer)\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Ernest Cole</a>’s glimpse into South African life under apartheid and <a href=\"http://www.lademiddel.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Cristina de Middel</a>’s piece that captures a Tijuana pole vaulter mid-air—and shop the <a href=\"https://www.magnumphotos.com/shop/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">full collection</a> before the sale ends at 6 p.m. EST on August 6.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div id=\"attachment_132838\" style=\"width: 1261px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-132838\" class=\"wp-image-132838 size-full\" src=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/magnum-13.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1251\" height=\"832\" srcset=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/magnum-13.jpg 1251w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/magnum-13-640x426.jpg 640w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/magnum-13-960x638.jpg 960w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/magnum-13-768x511.jpg 768w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/magnum-13-624x415.jpg 624w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/magnum-13-624x415@2x.jpg 1248w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1251px) 100vw, 1251px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-132838\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Alex Webb/Magnum Photos. 19:43:40","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:43:40","title":"A Drawing Machine Linked to A Synthesizer Audiates Geometric Illustrations by Musician Lamond Campbell","link":"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/?p=132991","description":"<p><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/HbKzrA_BJm4\" width=\"960\" height=\"540\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"><span data-mce-type=\"bookmark\" style=\"display: inline-block; width: 0px; overflow: hidden; line-height: 0;\" class=\"mce_SELRES_start\">﻿</span><span data-mce-type=\"bookmark\" style=\"display: inline-block; width: 0px; overflow: hidden; line-height: 0;\" class=\"mce_SELRES_start\">﻿</span></iframe></p>\n<p>Beyond the scratch of the pen on paper, drawing as a practice isn&#8217;t thought to be particularly rhythmic or melodic. An inventive machine by musician <a href=\"https://www.lomondcampbell.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Lamond Campbell</a>, though, adds a musical component to its looped sketches. <a href=\"https://www.lomondcampbell.com/harmonograph\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Harmonograph Synthesiser</a> is exactly as its name suggests: Campbell connected a modern, modular synthesizer to an 18th-Century <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmonograph\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">harmonograph</a>, an antiquated apparatus that uses pendulums to render geometric shapes. Two of the swinging mechanisms move linearly with the pen, while the third rotates with the board. Each triggers the synthesizer when movement occurs, which creates the corresponding audio track. An additional microphone picks up the noise of the pen.</p>\n<p>Watch the video above to see the intricacies of the modified contraption. Campell is selling a complete, 18-track collection on his site, and you can find more about his multi-media creations on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/lomond_campbell/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a> and <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCXyqsJ-AycDjNc4qWEUDbpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">YouTube</a>. To see a reverse audio-visual process, check out &#8220;<a href=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/2020/07/andy-thomas-visual-sounds-amazon/\">Visual Sounds of the Amazon II</a>.&#8221; <em>(thnx, Craig!)</em></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-132999\" src=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/campbell-2.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">All images © Chang Wan-ji and Hsu Sho-er, shared with permission</p></div>\n<p>Many of us fret over the loss of a beloved sweater or discovering a lone sock, but we can at least find some solace in knowing that the garments abandoned at Wansho Laundry in central Taiwan are being worn to their full potential. The laundromat&#8217;s owners, 83-year-old Chang Wan-ji and 84-year-old Hsu Sho-er, have been fashioning the skirts, blouses, and trousers left behind into adorable, eclectic styles. Just last month, their grandson Chang Reef began sharing photographs of the octogenarian couple modeling their fashionable outfits—which often include matching shoes, graphic tees, and a range of accessories like hats, big sunglasses, and small leather pouches—on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CC2XcYbnFEh/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a>, where they&#8217;ve since gone viral. For more of Chang and Hsu&#8217;s backstory (they got married in 1959!), dive into <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/07/24/world/asia/taiwan-octogenarian-couple-instagram-laundry.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">this <em>New York Times</em> profile</a>. (via <a href=\"https://kottke.org/20/07/cute-laundry-shop-couple-stylishly-models-clothes-left-behind-by-their-patrons\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Kottke</a>)</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-133037\" src=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/want-show-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"mce_SELRES_start\">﻿</span></iframe></p>\n<p>From gurgling liquids to crackling fire to rainbow-colored fur, a range of materials envelop an indistinct figure in <a href=\"https://universaleverything.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Universal Everything</a>’s new animation. &#8220;<a href=\"https://universaleverything.com/projects/transfiguration-2020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Transfiguration</a>&#8221; follows a central character as it wades across the screen wearing full-coverage suits that evolve with each step. Despite the mesmerizing changes in appearance, the figure never walks farther than mid-frame.</p>\n<p>To create this new, CGI animation, Universal Everything (<a href=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/?s=%22Universal+Everything%22\">previously</a>) updated a similar piece from 2011. The United Kingdom-based art and design studio engages in a wide range of digital projects, which you can find on <a href=\"https://vimeo.com/universal\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Vimeo</a> and <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/universaleverything/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone src=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/aurora-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1069\" srcset=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/aurora-1.jpg https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/aurora-1-768x684.jpg 768w, https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/aurora-1-624x556.jpg 624w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Aurora is a story of a celestial voyage: inspired by NASA satellite footage, <a href=\"https://www.rclarkson.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Richard Clarkson Studio</a> sought to create a collection that captures the feeling of flying through space and witnessing the Aurora Australis as it dances above the earth. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Drawing from a palette of delicate greens, fuchsia, and blues, the design mimics the elegant melange of colors emitted during the phenomenon through translucent lights, opaque blacks, and clouded resin panels. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Comprised of a chandelier, linear suspension, pendants, sconces, and desk stand, the new <a href=\"https://www.rclarkson.com/pages/aurora\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Aurora Collection</a> is Richard Clarkson&#8217;s most ambitious lighting endeavor yet, allowing for use in a multitude of settings that range from residences to museums and large-scale event installations.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Released ahead of the rest of the collection, the <a href=\"https://www.rclarkson.com/products/aurora-sconce\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">sconce</a>, <a href=\"https://www.rclarkson.com/products/aurora-pendant\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">pendant</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.rclarkson.com/products/aurora-tabletop\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">tabletop</a> iterations each consist of two flowing shapes of resin, a dynamically animated LED light source, and an aluminum, matte, black reflector. With six different shapes and four color options, both the sconce and the pendant are adaptable to a number of different contexts.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For those interested in a minimal design, the studio offers a clear version of the resin panels, along with the standard options. It recommends overlapping differently hued panels or requesting custom colors for those who want a more vibrant and unique piece. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The flowing shapes of each panel also are able to be rotated independently of each other, allowing them to take on subtle changes in form. When installed in larger spaces, the lights should be placed in clusters of three or more. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><br />\n</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><br />\n</span>Shop the full collection on <a href=\"https://www.rclarkson.com/collections/shop\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Richard Clarkson Studio&#8217;s site</a>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/michele_volpi_2-624x672@2x.jpg 1248w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1440px) 100vw, 1440px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-132936\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">All images © Michele Volpi, shared with permission</p></div>\n<p>One might learn something from staring at the tattoos of Italian artist Michele Volpi (<a href=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/2019/12/surreal-tattoos-by-michele-volpi/\">previously</a>). The composition, detailed dot work, and precise lines of his tattoos transcend both ink-infused skin and science textbooks. The Bologna-based tattoo artist relishes in scientific books—from Frank Netter’s painterly medical illustrations to the exquisitely rendered biological specimens and marine life of <a href=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/2017/11/the-art-and-science-of-ernst-haeckel/\">Ernst Haeckel</a>. He often visits bookshops during his travels to discover and acquire these new sources of inspiration.</p>\n<p>Volpi&#8217;s customers seek him out to tattoo an array of botany, astronomy, physiology, and chemistry-based compositions. Sometimes customers let him choose the branch of science, in which case he renders his favorite subject—anatomy. Even then, Volpi combines subject matter like in his tattoo comparing the shape of a human pelvis to that of a butterfly or another that features a human skull being stretched absurdly through a wormhole.</p>\n<p>The artist tells Colossal that his “dream is to make a scientific book with all of my conceptual scientific illustrations that I love.” View Volpi’s body of work and booking information on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/_mfox/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Instagram</a>. For those not ready for the permanence of a tattoo, there are prints of his pen-and-ink, anatomical illustrations available in his <a href=\"https://michelevolpi.bigcartel.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">shop</a>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-132940 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.thisiscolossal.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/michele_volpi_9.jpg\"
